  ***** BEGIN IOP MODEL SPECIFICATIONS *****

     The IOP routine "abCASE2" is being used:

     Absorption and scattering coefficients for case 1 or 2 water are used.

        component 1 is pure water
        component 2 is pigmented particles (Chl)
        component 3 is CDOM (yellow matter)
        component 4 is mineral particles

     Pure water a and b values are obtained from the file:
        ..\data\H2OabDefaults_FRESHwater.txt                                                                                    
        (Linear interpolation is used to define values at all wavelengths)

     The data file header records from ..\data\H2OabDefaults_FRESHwater.txt are:
        Default "pure FRESH water" absorption (a) and scattering (b) coefficients. Based on:
        200-300 nm: R.C. Smith and K. Baker, 1981. Appl. Optics 20(2), 177-184.

        191 records read

     The phase function for component  1 comes from a file titled
     pure sea water (Rayleigh-like phase function); standard quad partition; 7 Sept 98

     The chlorophyll concentration is constant with depth with a value of     0.50 (mg/m^3)

     Specific Absorption for component 2 read in from file: ..\data\Examples\astarchl.txt                                                                                           

         91 records read

     Scattering for component 2 calculated using a Power Law model
          b = 0.3000 X^(0.6200) * (550./wavenm)^(1.0000)

     The phase function for component  2 will be chosen to have a bb/b ratio of   0.0050

     The CDOM absorption at each wavelength is constant with depth with a value of     0.50 (1/m)

     Specific Absorption for component 3 calculated from an Exponential model:
          astar(waven) = 1.0000* exp[ -0.0140*(waven - 440.)]

     The phase function for component  3 comes from a file titled
     isotropic phase function, betatilde = 1/(4 pi); standard quad partition; 7 Sept 98

     The mineral concentration is constant with depth with a value of     2.00 (g/m^3)


     Specific Absorption for component 4 read in from file: C:\HE53\data\defaults\astarmin_brownearth.txt                                                                           

        141 records read

     Specific scattering for component 4 read in from file: C:\HE53\data\defaults\bstarmin_brownearth.txt                                                                           

        141 records read

     The phase function for component  4 will be chosen to have a bb/b ratio of   0.0200

  ***** BEGIN INELASTIC SCATTER AND INTERNAL SOURCE SPECIFICATIONS *****

     Chlorophyll fluorescence is included in this run
        Chl fluorescent quantum efficiency set to  0.020

     CDOM fluorescence is included in this run

     Raman scattering is included in this run
        The Raman scattering cross section is 2.60E-04 1/m at reference wavelength  488.0 nm
        The Raman scattering cross section depends on the EXCITATION wavelength as (reference wavelength/excitation wavelength)^5.30

  ***** END INELASTIC SCATTER AND INTERNAL SOURCE SPECIFICATIONS *****


  ***** BEGIN ATMOSPHERIC MODEL SPECIFICATIONS *****

     Normalized sky radiances are computed using sky model "HCNRAD" (Harrison and Coombes Normalized RADiances)
        The cloud fraction is cloud =  0.0 (0 for a clear sky to 1 for a heavy overcast)

     The sun is placed in quad Q(r,s) = Q( 6, 1) centered at (theta, phi) = (40.000,  0.000)


     The data file header records from C:\HE53\data\User\FullMoonEdtot.txt are:
        Lunar irradiance spectrum based on http://www.olino.org/us/articles/2015/10/05/spectrum-of-moon-light
        This is a full moon radiance or luminance spectrum rescaled to give Ed(400-700) approx = 1e-3 W/m2, as in L&W Table 1.4
        3

        751 records read


     The incident total (direct + diffuse) sky irradiance is obtained from user data file: 

        C:\HE53\data\User\FullMoonEdtot.txt

     Gregg and Carder values used to get the ratio of diffuse to direct irradiance

     Diffuse and Direct Sky irradiances are computed using the "RADTRANX" (RADTRAN eXtended for 300-1000 nm) model
     The RADTRAN clear-sky irradiances are adjusted for cloudiness by the model of Kasten and Czeplak

     Parameter values used in the RADTRANX model:
          Solar zenith angle =   40.0  degrees
          Pressure           =   29.9  in. mercury
          Day of year        =  not set (mean earth-sun distance used)
          Air mass type      =    1.0
          Relative Humidity  =   80.0  %
          Precipitable water =    2.5  cm
          24-hr wind speed   =    5.0  m/sec
          Current wind speed =    5.0  m/sec
          Visibility         =   15.0  km
          Total ozone        =  300.0  Dobson units

     Irradiances are computed just above the sea surface

     Aerosol optical thickness at 550 nm =    0.261
